**Generated:** 2026-04-25

**Section tasks:** 53
**Context mode:** full source section embedded in every task; no excerpt truncation.
**Quality threshold:** every task must score at least 9.5/10 before implementation begins.

## Purpose
Turn every dashboard PRD section into explicit backend-support work. Even visual/frontend sections must produce backend projection, telemetry, fixture, schema, or explicit no-backend rationale so frontend implementation is easy and stable.

## Global Implementation Rules
- Extend existing modules before creating new ones; only add new route/service files when no canonical owner exists.
- Implement production wiring, not only structs, mocks, or isolated helpers.
- Preserve every extracted detail unless a parity-ledger row explicitly marks it covered or deferred.
- Add persistence, events, auth/safety, dashboard projections, and docs updates whenever the requirement reaches those surfaces.
- A checked box means code, tests, docs, parity ledger, and strict gates are done for that task.

## Primary Target Areas
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/meta.rs`
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/projections.rs`
- `crates/roko-learn/src/adas.rs`

- Runtime: wire into the production agent loop with lifecycle, cancellation, health, audit, provider/tool safety, and observable events.
- Frontend support: provide stable projections, mock fixtures, empty/loading/stale/degraded/unauthorized states, and realtime update payloads that match projection schemas.
- Config/deployment: validate defaults, hot reload or restart-required paths, env var diagnostics, service dry-runs, and non-destructive operations.

### DASH-16-S002 -- Section overview

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/16-meta-surfaces.md:7` through `27`
**Heading level:** H2
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
## Section overview

Meta is the section where the product's most ambitious thesis — tools for tools, recursion as the engine of improvement — becomes concrete. Here users create agents that create agents, evals that evaluate evals, generators that generate generators. This is where thesis 8 from `02-theses-and-principles.md` lives in the UI.

Meta is a new top-level sidebar section in this specification. It does not exist in the current dashboard. Making it a first-class section is a deliberate choice — meta work is normal work, per the thesis, and the UI should treat it as such rather than hiding it in an advanced-settings menu.

Meta is classified as a Tier 3 section (hidden by default for new users, revealed when they navigate to it or create their first meta-object). But once revealed, it behaves like every other section of the dashboard.

Meta contains four pages:

- **Meta-Agents** — create, operate, inspect meta-agents. An agent that produces other agents for specific task categories.
- **Generator Studio** — build generators for new first-class objects: extensions, arenas, domains, gates, evals.
- **Recursive Workshop** — observe recursive behavior safely. Trace lineage across multiple layers. Inspect what a meta-agent produced and why.
- **Meta-Lineage** — genealogy of objects in the system. Which agents produced which; which evals retired which; which generators spawned which.

Primary persona for Meta: Meta-Builder (primary resident). Secondary: Domain Architect (for domain generators), System Steward (for system integrity of recursive behavior), any advanced user exploring the recursive layer.

The design challenge for Meta is to make recursion interpretable. Recursion that is opaque is scary — users won't trust what they can't see. The Meta surfaces must expose, at every level, what is happening, what is being produced, and why.

---
````

**Explicit detail extraction from this section:**

- Meta is a new top-level sidebar section in this specification. It does not exist in the current dashboard. Making it a first-class section is a deliberate choice — meta work is normal work, per the thesis, and the UI should treat it as such rather than hiding it in an advanced-settings menu.
- Meta is classified as a Tier 3 section (hidden by default for new users, revealed when they navigate to it or create their first meta-object). But once revealed, it behaves like every other section of the dashboard.
- - **Meta-Agents** — create, operate, inspect meta-agents. An agent that produces other agents for specific task categories. - **Generator Studio** — build generators for new first-class objects: extensions, arenas, domains, gates, evals. - **Recursive Workshop** — observe recursive behavior safely. ### DASH-16-S004 -- Purpose

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/16-meta-surfaces.md:30` through `35`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Purpose

Where users create, operate, and inspect meta-agents. A meta-agent is an agent whose task is producing other agents. It takes a specification — a task, a goal, a domain — and produces a configured agent appropriate to the specification.

Meta-agents are still agents. They have domains, extensions, gates, model routing, knowledge stores, reputations. What distinguishes them is that their output is other agents. A meta-agent's capabilities include agent-creation tools (defining domain configs, selecting extensions, setting gate pipelines, etc.).
````

### DASH-16-S008 -- Page sections

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/16-meta-surfaces.md:51` through `100`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `auth`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page sections

**Section 00 — Meta-Agents header.**

Title, italic-serif description: *"Agents that create agents. The recursive engine of the system. Every meta-agent is still an agent — with the added ability to produce others."*

CTAs: "Create a meta-agent" (primary), "Fork a public meta-agent" (secondary).

**Section 01 — My meta-agents.**

A list of the user's meta-agents. Each shown as a specialized card:

- Agent portrait (with a distinct visual indicator that this is a meta-agent — a double-layered glyph, a subtle orbital pattern).
- Meta-agent name.
- Target specification (what kinds of agents it produces).
- Children count (how many agents it has produced).
- Average child success rate (measured by external evals of the children).
- Current state (active, idle, paused).
- Last generation timestamp.

Clicking navigates to Meta-Agent Detail (which is Agent Detail with additional meta-specific sections).

**Section 02 — Recent generations.**

A timeline (primitive 12) showing recent generations. Each generation marker shows:

- Meta-agent that produced.
- Child agent produced.
- Specification used.
- Outcome (if known).

Timeline is live — new generations appear as meta-agents produce.

**Section 03 — Featured public meta-agents.**

A curated list of notable meta-agents on the network. Each shown with:

- Name.
- Creator.
- Target specification.
- Total descendants.
- Aggregate child success rate.
- Fork button.

Users can fork any public meta-agent to adapt its approach.

**Section 04 — Create new meta-agent.**

A prominent section (or CTA leading to a dedicated authoring page, specified in `19-authoring-surfaces.md`). Calls out: "Build a meta-agent that produces [type of agent] for [domain]."
````

### DASH-16-S016 -- Purpose

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/16-meta-surfaces.md:143` through `148`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Purpose

Where users build generators for first-class objects other than agents: new extensions, new arenas, new domains, new gates, new evals. A generator is like a meta-agent but produces a specific type of non-agent object.

Generators expand the product's recursion to cover more than just agent creation. An arena generator can produce new arenas on demand. A gate generator can produce new gates tailored to specific contexts. An eval generator can produce new evals as the system discovers new measurable quantities.
````

- Storage: define deterministic schema, migration/default behavior, corruption handling, restart recovery, cleanup/GC, and fixture data.
- Chain: default to devnet/simulation, prove contract/client/indexer sync, enforce wallet/risk/simulation gates, and record audit/witness data.
- Runtime: wire into the production agent loop with lifecycle, cancellation, health, audit, provider/tool safety, and observable events.
- Frontend support: provide stable projections, mock fixtures, empty/loading/stale/degraded/unauthorized states, and realtime update payloads that match projection schemas.
- Verification: add deterministic unit, integration, route/CLI, auth/safety, persistence/restart, serialization, and failing-path tests; avoid LLM self-grading where ground truth is required.
- Config/deployment: validate defaults, hot reload or restart-required paths, env var diagnostics, service dry-runs, and non-destructive operations.

**Explicit implementation obligations derived from this section:**
- [ ] Implement or verify `of` in the canonical crate with serde/validation/defaults where it is a data type, and unit tests for boundary behavior.
- [ ] For this dashboard-derived task, prefer backend projection/realtime support over frontend stitching: one stable payload, typed stale/degraded states, and fixtures for local UI development.

````markdown
### Page sections

**Section 00 — Generator Studio header.**

- Extension Generators.
- Arena Generators.
- Domain Generators.
- Gate Generators.
- Eval Generators.
- (Extensible for future types.)

Each tab shows:

- User's generators of that type.
- Recent outputs (objects produced).
- Public generators available for forking.

**Section 02 — Featured generators.**

A spotlight on generators that have produced notable outputs. A domain generator whose produced domains are widely adopted; an eval generator whose produced evals are well-calibrated and used.

**Section 03 — Recent outputs.**

A feed of recently generated objects across all generator types. Users can see what the network is producing.
````

````markdown
### Deferred

- Generator composition: generators that compose multiple generators. Recursive by nature; deferred as a dedicated feature.
- Auto-publishing: generators that automatically publish their outputs to the network. Manual publishing default; auto-publish with caveats deferred.
- Generator evals: evals that evaluate generators (how good is this generator at producing good outputs?). Part of Meta-Evals; explicit generator evals deferred.

---
````

- Chain: default to devnet/simulation, prove contract/client/indexer sync, enforce wallet/risk/simulation gates, and record audit/witness data.
- Frontend support: provide stable projections, mock fixtures, empty/loading/stale/degraded/unauthorized states, and realtime update payloads that match projection schemas.
- Verification: add deterministic unit, integration, route/CLI, auth/safety, persistence/restart, serialization, and failing-path tests; avoid LLM self-grading where ground truth is required.
- Config/deployment: validate defaults, hot reload or restart-required paths, env var diagnostics, service dry-runs, and non-destructive operations.

### DASH-16-S028 -- Purpose

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/16-meta-surfaces.md:237` through `242`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Purpose

Where users safely observe recursive behavior. When meta-agents run, generators produce, and children improve on parents, things can happen fast. Recursive Workshop is the observation surface that makes this traceable and auditable.

This page is the answer to the "what is my meta-agent doing" question. It is critical for the interpretability of the meta layer.
````

### DASH-16-S032 -- Page sections

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/16-meta-surfaces.md:259` through `314`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `auth`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page sections

**Section 00 — Recursive Workshop header.**

Title, italic-serif description: *"Observe the recursion. Every child, every generation, every lineage."*

**Section 01 — Active recursive processes.**

A list of currently-running recursive processes:

- Meta-agent generating children.
- Generator producing outputs.
- Chained meta-agent (meta-agent produces meta-agent produces agent).

Each shown with:

- Process name.
- Depth (how many recursive layers deep).
- Child count so far.
- Rate of generation.
- Safety indicators (any caveats triggered, any outputs flagged).
- Controls: pause, inspect, cancel.

**Section 02 — Recent recursive outputs.**

A timeline showing recent outputs. Each output has:

- Level (depth in the recursion).
- Parent (what produced it).
- Child (what was produced).
- Specification (what the parent was asked to produce).
- Outcome (success, failure, pending).

**Section 03 — Safety watch.**

A panel focused on safety signals:

- Caveat violations (meta-agent produced something outside its scope).
- Rate anomalies (sudden spike in generation rate).
- Quality anomalies (sudden drop in child success rate).
- Circular generations (meta-agent produces a meta-agent that produces the first one).

Each anomaly shown with severity, detail, and action (investigate, pause, quarantine).

**Section 04 — Traceability.**

For any selected recursive process or output, a detailed trace view:

- Full chain of cause and effect.
- Specifications at each layer.
- Decisions made.
- LLM calls and contexts used.
- Tool invocations.

This is the "why did this happen" panel.
````

````markdown
### Deferred

- Custom safety rules: users define their own anomaly-detection rules for recursive processes. Deferred.
- Automatic quarantine: generators that misbehave are automatically paused. Manual control default; auto-quarantine deferred.
- Cross-user recursive traces: seeing how the user's generators affect the broader network. Partial via Global Lens; dedicated cross-user tools deferred.

---
````

### DASH-16-S040 -- Purpose

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/16-meta-surfaces.md:358` through `363`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Purpose

The genealogy of objects in the system. Every agent, eval, arena, extension, gate, domain has a creation history — produced by a generator, forked from a template, evolved from a parent. Meta-Lineage makes these histories navigable.

This is where a user can answer: "Where did this agent come from?" "What agents are descended from this meta-agent?" "Which eval retired this older eval?" "Which domain is the ancestor of this domain?"
````

### DASH-16-S044 -- Page sections

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/16-meta-surfaces.md:380` through `427`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page sections

**Section 00 — Meta-Lineage header.**

Title, italic-serif description: *"Every agent has parents. Every arena has ancestors. The genealogy of the system, navigable."*

**Section 01 — Lineage graph.**

The primary visualization. A graph showing nodes (objects) connected by generation edges (parent → child relationships). Uses the generic Field primitive (primitive 13) or a dedicated tree visualization.

Nodes colored by type (agent, eval, arena, etc.). Edges colored by relationship (generated, forked, evolved).

The user can pan, zoom, click a node to see its details. Clicking a node can also re-root the visualization at that node.

Layout options:

- Tree (hierarchical, good for clear parent-child).
- Force-directed (good for complex graphs with multiple parents).
- Timeline (good for seeing generation order).

**Section 02 — Most-copied / most-forked.**

A leaderboard-style list of the most copied or forked objects in the network. Each shows:

- Object name.
- Type.
- Descendants count.
- Forks count.
- Creator.

This surfaces influential objects — the meta-agents, domains, arenas, or evals that have spawned the most subsequent work.

**Section 03 — Filter and search.**

- Object type filter (agents only, evals only, arenas only, etc.).
- Time window (when created, when descended).
- Domain filter.
- Depth filter (show only N generations from a root).

**Section 04 — Lineage traces (on selection).**

When a user clicks a node, a side panel shows:

- Full ancestor chain (this object's parents, grandparents, etc.).
- Full descendant tree.
- Generation events (when each child was produced).
- Notable branches.
````

````markdown
### Interactions

- Click a node: select it, show detail panel.
````

### DASH-16-S051 -- Shared patterns across Meta

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/16-meta-surfaces.md:473` through `488`
**Heading level:** H2
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
## Shared patterns across Meta

**Everything in Meta exposes its lineage.** Agents, generators, meta-agents, arenas, and evals created through Meta surfaces always have clear provenance. Users can always answer "where did this come from."

**Safety signals are everywhere.** Meta surfaces surface safety anomalies prominently. Users never need to hunt for "is this meta-agent misbehaving?" The answer is on screen or one click away.

**Recursion is visible, not magical.** The dashboard never hides how meta-objects work. A meta-agent is an agent; its tools, gates, and decisions are inspectable like any other agent's.

**Meta is Tier 3 but normal.** The section is hidden by default for new users, but when revealed, it is a full peer to every other section. No simplified mode, no "meta mode" that is different from the base dashboard — just normal UI applied to recursive work.

**Forks preserve lineage.** When a user forks a public meta-agent or generator, the fork records its ancestor. Users can see "this is a fork of X" and navigate to X. Lineage is preserved even across users.

**Caveats are enforced at every level.** A meta-agent's caveats apply to its children. A generator's caveats apply to what it produces. Users can inspect and edit caveats at each level (under System → Delegations).

---
````

**Explicit detail extraction from this section:**

- Section word count: `211`
- Section hash: `98d9945bcf36f2febad8c8d58a026c1bb6c22ecab03080a9a320608d05dd4d2c`

**Normative requirements and implementation claims:**
- **Everything in Meta exposes its lineage.** Agents, generators, meta-agents, arenas, and evals created through Meta surfaces always have clear provenance. Users can always answer "where did this come from."
- **Safety signals are everywhere.** Meta surfaces surface safety anomalies prominently. Users never need to hunt for "is this meta-agent misbehaving?" The answer is on screen or one click away.
- **Recursion is visible, not magical.** The dashboard never hides how meta-objects work. A meta-agent is an agent; its tools, gates, and decisions are inspectable like any other agent's.
- **Meta is Tier 3 but normal.** The section is hidden by default for new users, but when revealed, it is a full peer to every other section. No simplified mode, no "meta mode" that is different from the base dashboard — just normal UI applied to recursive work.
- **Forks preserve lineage.** When a user forks a public meta-agent or generator, the fork records its ancestor. Users can see "this is a fork of X" and navigate to X. Lineage is preserved even across users.
- **Caveats are enforced at every level.** A meta-agent's caveats apply to its children. A generator's caveats apply to what it produces. Users can inspect and edit caveats at each level (under System → Delegations).

### DASH-16-S052 -- Deferred across Meta

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
## Deferred across Meta

- **Dedicated meta-evals surface beyond the one in Measurements.** Meta-Evals as a concept lives in `18-system-surfaces.md` under Measurements. A more extensive meta-eval workbench is deferred.
- **Collaborative meta-construction.** Multiple users working together on a meta-agent or generator. Deferred to collaboration features workstream.
- **Meta-agent versioning.** Pinning to a specific version of a meta-agent for stable descendant production. Basic versioning included; rich version control deferred.
- **Constitutional meta-agents.** Meta-agents whose behavior is governed by a set of rules they cannot violate (a "constitution"). Basic caveats exist; constitutional framework deferred.
- **Swarm meta-agents.** A meta-agent that produces many agents simultaneously, coordinated as a swarm. Basic production supported; explicit swarm tooling deferred.
- **Meta-economic surfaces.** Meta-agents that produce agents that generate revenue, with revenue-sharing back to meta-agent owners. Deferred to economic-features workstream.

---
````

### DASH-16-S053 -- A note on tone

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/16-meta-surfaces.md:500` through `508`
**Heading level:** H2
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
## A note on tone

Meta surfaces risk feeling clinical or esoteric. They are deep conceptual territory. To keep them usable, the specifications favor visible language over abstract jargon:

- "Meta-agent" is sometimes abstract; the surface uses "agents that create agents" wherever possible.
- "Generator" pairs with "produces new [thing]" to stay concrete.
- "Lineage" uses "parents," "descendants," "forks" instead of "nodes" and "edges" in user-facing copy.

The goal is that a user approaching Meta for the first time can understand what is happening without a dictionary. Power users get the concepts; new users get the plain language.
````
